[2109] Chapter Twenty-Four
[2110] Catastrophe and Discovery
[2111] The house became a smoky ruin ravaged by fire. Thick yellow smoke still hung on the nearby charred branches, and the air was filled with a choking smell of sulfur. The old wooden buildings were reduced to rubble, and fragments of walls and roofs littered the roads. The house collapsed on top of the cellar, and smoke still rose from the ash-covered ground. State troopers pushed their way through the curious crowd gathering around. The firefighters of Tarrytown had brought the fire under control and were now focusing on preventing the fire from spreading to the dry wood. The water supply for the fire engines was insufficient, so additional water tanks had to be brought in from Tarrytown and Ewington.
[2112] Officer Pauling met Perkins, Rowe, and Rayne at the edge of the open space. His ruddy face was covered in soot, and he was panting heavily. He roared, "Damn it! My two men are badly injured. Luckily, no one was inside when it happened. It exploded at six o'clock."
[2113] "No warning?" Rayne asked, showing signs of excitement, "I don't think it was a bomb dropped from a plane, right?"
[2114] "Impossible. There hasn't been a single plane flying overhead all day. My two men said that no one came near the house for an hour or two after we left."
[2115] "So it must have been a bomb placed inside the house beforehand," Rowe said gloomily. "Thank goodness it didn't go off earlier. What a close call!"
[2116] "We could have been here when it exploded—" Perkins' face turned pale, "This—this is hard to believe. A bomb!"
[2117] "It could have been in the cellar," Lane said indifferently, "We didn't search there this afternoon. What an idiotic oversight!"
[2118] "The cellar—I suppose that's where it was," Bowlin grumbled, "Well, my men need to be taken to the hospital. I'll go check on them. They were almost blown to pieces. We'll come back tomorrow when the fire is completely out."
[2119] The three sat quietly in the old gentleman's car on the way back to Hamlet Manor, lost in their own thoughts. Rowe seemed particularly absorbed, with his fingers on his lower lip and his gaze fixed on the sky.
[2120] "You know," Rowe suddenly spoke up, "I was thinking—"
[2121] "What?" Perkins said.
[2122] "It seems like there's a group of people involved in this. Without a doubt, that Shakespeare document, whatever it is, must be the key. I think Dr. Alessi found it in the Jagger of 1599 that he stole from the museum, making him one of the main players. The other one is the guy who was waving an axe around last night, if he wasn't after the document, what was he? That's point two. Another person arrived after the ax-wielder, and he didn't close the secret cabinet door, that's point three. Now there's this explosion, someone planted a bomb, that's point four, God, that's enough to give you a headache."
[2123] "Maybe not." Perkins argued, "The main players you mentioned - you're so technical - could be the same person. The second person to enter the house could have been Dr. Alessi, making the number three. The ax-wielder could have been the one who planted the bomb, leaving only two - Gordon, I'm going on like this, but there's one thing that's important. Now that I have time to think about this awful explosion, I have a very strange idea."
[2124] The fog in Reine's eyes cleared, replaced by a look of curiosity.
[2125] "We've been assuming that the person chasing the document wanted the document itself - stealing, owning, preserving it, all for the money - a common criminal motive."
[2126] Rowe chuckled. "Patty, you talk fresh! Of course, the motivation for digging up something valuable is usually like that, and that's a normal explanation."
[2127] Pechin sighed. "Maybe I'm crazy, but I can't help thinking that if the bomb was placed last night, the person who put it there probably knew the document was in the house!"
[2128] The old gentleman blinked. "Is that so, Pechin?"
[2129] "Oh, I think it's crazy, but we're dealing with extreme acts of violence - gunshots, theft, explosions... Only Maxwell was in the house, so the person who set the bomb must have known that. If you think the target of that bomb was the harmless old servant, that's absurd. If it wasn't him, who or what was it? We always thought the person or people chasing the document would keep it. Tell you, someone's goal was to destroy it!"
[2130] Rowe paused for a moment, then threw his head back and bit his teeth. "Oh, Patty, you're my nemesis. When it comes to women's arguments..." He rubbed his eyes. "What kind of bad guy wants to destroy a document with such a historical and monetary value? Who's so crazy!"
[2131] Pensin blushed. "I think you're annoying."
[2132] "Gordon, Pensin's reasoning is very logical." Ryan quickly chimed in, "Child, you can't outsmart this lady. I think if the document had only Shakespeare's signature, only a madman would destroy it. But if there's more to it than just the signature, the person who put the bomb definitely doesn't want the public to know what's on it, whatever it is."
[2133] "Well, what do you think, self-proclaimed genius?" Pensin said.
[2134] "But to destroy -" Luo Wei frowned, "I can't imagine what secret Shakespeare would write that would make people in the 20th century go to great lengths to cover up. What is it? It doesn't make sense!"
[2135] "That's the point." Ryan said coldly, "What is it? If you know - as for whether it makes sense or not, that's another matter."
[2136] If asked about Pechin, she might say that after this day, nothing would surprise her anymore. Looking back, the day started with a strange phone call, followed by a series of strange events – an old man attacked, a house mysteriously destroyed, and ended with a terrible explosion. Little did she know, there were still things waiting for her, Roe, and Raine at Hamlet Manor.
[2137] As the sky darkened, the drawbridge was lit up, and the old face of Quincy shone brightly in front of the ancient lanterns.
[2138] "Mr. Jules!" he called. "Is anyone hurt?"
[2139] "Not seriously, Quincy. What's going on?"
[2140] "There's someone in the hall who wants to see you. He called as soon as you left. He seemed very upset, Mr. Jules."
[2141] "Who is it?"
[2142] "He said his name is Jot."
[2143] They hurried towards the hall. The entire manor was designed to resemble a medieval British castle, and the layout of the hall echoed the past. Standing at a distance, with his hands behind his back, was the director of the British Museum, Dr. Jot, pacing under the tragic mask that Rowe had carefully placed at one end of the hall.
[2144] The three of them rushed towards him.
[2145] "Dr. Jot," Rowe said slowly, "I apologize for keeping you waiting. There were some unexpected events... Your face looks as grim as that mask. What's the matter?"
[2146] "Unexpected events?" Dr. Jotter said angrily. "So you know about it?" He nodded reluctantly at Percy and Rowe.
[2147] "The explosion?"
[2148] "Explosion? What explosion? Oh, no! I mean Dr. Sedra."
[2149] "Dr. Sedra!" The three of them exclaimed.
[2150] "He's missing."
[2151] The librarian leans against an oak table, with bloodshot eyes.
[2152] "Missing?" Percy furrows his brow, "How could that be? We saw him on Saturday, didn't we, Gordon?"
[2153] "Yes, indeed." The librarian rumbles, "He came in on Saturday morning and stayed for a few minutes, seemed fine. Before he left, I asked him to call me at home on Sunday – last night – to discuss some museum matters. He agreed and left."
[2154] "He didn't call?" Raine whispers.
[2155] "No. I contacted the Seneca Inn where he was staying, and he wasn't there. I waited for him all day today, hoping he'd get in touch, but nothing. Dr. Jotter shrugs, "It's – it's stupid! He didn't say he was leaving. I thought maybe he was sick, so I called the inn again this afternoon. They said they haven't seen him since Saturday morning."
[2156] "That doesn't mean he disappeared Saturday!" Rowe countered.
[2157] "I know. It's just strange. I don't know what to do. Should I call the police or… I tried to reach your father, Miss Samuels, but the office secretary said…"
[2158] "First Donoho, then Dr. Aless, and now Sedra," Percy lamented. "These people are disappearing one by one! It's – it's unacceptable!"
[2159] "Unless Sedra is Aless," Rowe said.
[2160] Dr. Jotter ran his fingers through his hair. "Oh, my God!"
[2161] Pinchot frowned. "I don't think that necessarily means Dr. Aless is Sedra, or that he escaped with the file."
[2162] "Dear Miss Sampson, the hotel staff said all of his things were still in the room. I don't think a person running away would do that. What file are you talking about—"
[2163] Raine looked exhausted, with deep circles under his eyes and skin that looked like crumpled parchment. He wearily shook his head: "These conjectures won't get us anywhere. It's a surprising turn of events… The only thing I can suggest is to find out what happened to Sedra."
[2164] Pinchot and Roebling arrived in town late at night. They parked their car outside the Seneca Hotel and went inside to find the manager. After some hesitation, they were granted permission to look at Dr. Sedra's room. The room seemed tidy, with British-cut clothes neatly hanging in the closet, freshly laundered sheets and pillowcases in the dresser, and three unopened suitcases and bags. The manager seemed reluctant to involve the police, glancing at Pinchot's credentials—which, of course, were the detective's—and reluctantly allowing the search of the room.
[2165] The luggage and clothes were all British. There were some letters in the room, with postmarks from "London" and addressed to Dr. Hamnett Sedra, apparently from former British colleagues. The passport and visa were in order, issued to Dr. Hamnett Sedra, with a familiar-looking photo attached.
[2166] "It's Sedra, no doubt," Rowe said grimly. "I'm starting to get paranoid about this. There's no sign here that this person wanted to flee the country."
[2167] "Ugh!" Peachins muttered under his breath. "Gordon, take me home, and—and, kiss me!"
[2168] Chapter 25
[2169] Murder
[2170] The sun shone brightly. The fire had been extinguished, and the smoke had dispersed with the night, leaving only burnt-out ashes, piles of rubble, and charred trees to bear witness to the explosion of the night before. Firefighters and police were busy digging through the rubble. A dark-skinned man calmly directed the entire operation, his eyes sharp and eager to clear away the debris so he could descend into the cellar to see what was inside.
[2171] They stood by the edge of the woods, the warm morning breeze rustling their clothes. Pauling watched the workers with a cold eye.
[2172] "See that guy with the hawk eyes? He's an explosives expert. I think since he's involved, he should do a good job! I want to see how this strange thing happened."
[2173] "You mean he'll find something in that pile of garbage?" Roeve asked.
[2174] "That's why he's here."
[2175] The workers made rapid progress, quickly clearing the debris blocking the cave. They shoveled the garbage to thirty feet away, hand over hand. Once the cellar was almost clear enough to descend, the silent man crawled into the hole and disappeared. Ten minutes later, he reappeared, looking around as if measuring the extent of the explosion, and then disappeared again, this time into the woods. He reappeared again and descended into the cellar. The third time he emerged, he wore a satisfied expression, holding in his hands a jumbled mess of iron pieces, rubber, glass, and wires.
[2176] "How's it going?" Pauling asked.
[2177] "Sir, the evidence is here." The explosives expert said, picking up a fragment of a clock-like instrument, "A time bomb."
[2178] "Ah!" Mr. Philo Vance said.
[2179] "Primitive, homemade. Set to go off at six o'clock with yellow dynamite."
[2180] Percy, Roe, and Vance all thought the same thing, but Vance was the first to ask: "When was the bomb placed?"
[2181] "At six o'clock on Sunday evening - if the bomb went off last night at six o'clock. It's a twenty-four-hour timer."
[2182] "Six o'clock on Sunday evening." Perkins repeated slowly, "So it was put on before Maxwell was attacked on Sunday night!"
[2183] "You're right, Perri." Rowe said, "If the person who put the bomb knew there were documents in the house, his purpose was to destroy the documents, so he knew the stuff was in the house but didn't know exactly where. It's difficult -"
[2184] "The epicenter of the explosion was the cellar." The expert spat on the charred rock.
[2185] Reine let out another "Ah."
[2186] "The second visitor – the one who took the documents out of the secret cabinet –" Perkins looked pointedly at Reen, "could not have been the one who planted the bomb. It's obvious. The second visitor knew where the documents were; the bomber didn't, as you said, Gordon…" Perkins' words were interrupted by a coarse roar, coming from the workers digging through the cellar debris. They all turned around.
[2187] "What is it?" Bowlin called, running over quickly.
[2188] Three people were bending over something, their heads almost touching. One of them turned around, pale and trembling. He managed to speak: "Sir, there's a body here. From the look on his face, he was – murdered."
[2189] The young man ran towards the edge of the house foundation, stepping on black ash. Reen followed slowly, his face pale and anxious.
[2190] Roarke looked at the scene in front of him and roughly pushed Perkins aside. "Petty, get away from here," he said hoarsely. "You'd better go stand under that tree over there. This – it's not good."
[2191] "Oh," Perkins said. Her nostrils flared, and she silently obeyed his request.
[2192] The men all widened their eyes and focused intently on the deep hole. A young, red-faced policeman crawled out from the corner of the cellar, bent over, and began to shake and vomit... The body was badly burned, almost unrecognizable - one leg and one arm were missing, and the clothes were completely burnt.
[2193] "How do you know he was murdered?" Reen asked sternly.
[2194] An older policeman's mouth twisted: "He's not completely burnt, I can see the hole."
[2195] "Hole?" Rowe croaked.
[2196] The man sighed. "Three holes. In his stomach, clean and neat. Those are bullet holes, sir, don't forget."
[2197] Three hours later, Raine, Detective Bolling, Peachins, and the young Roe sat silently in the office of the Prosecutor of Tarrytown. Someone had called to dispatch a car to take the body to the morgue in Tarrytown. Apart from the usual procedures of collecting the remains and their belongings, Bolling ordered no one to touch the body. The officers searched for fragments of the clothing, hoping to find buttons that could provide clues to the victim's identity. However, the explosion had damaged the body so much that the officer soon gave up searching. The explosives expert happily said that the body was not turned into atoms, a miracle.
[2198] They sat at the prosecutor's desk, staring at the items on the table. This was the only item taken from under the body that could be used as a clue – a cheap British-made watch with a leather strap. If traced back to its source, it would be a waste of time. The watch case was almost gone, leaving only a small triangular piece of glass. The synthetic metal used to make the watch, despite its surface turning gray-black, was not damaged by the explosion. There was one strange thing: the hands pointed to 12:26; the face of the watch had a deep cut that went over the number "10" and extended to the edge of the watch.
[2199] "That's odd," the prosecutor, a young man with worried eyes, said. "Bolling, didn't you tell me the body was found face down, with the arm wearing this watch pressed under the stomach?"
[2200] "Yes."
[2201] "Then the cut on the case of the watch was not left by the explosion."
[2202] "There are other suspicious things," Percy said. "If the watch stopped because of the explosion, the pointer should have stopped at six o'clock, but it didn't."
[2203] The prosecutor looked at her approvingly. "Right! I didn't even think of it myself. You're Sam Chief's daughter, aren't you?"
[2204] The coroner rushed in - a short, bald man with a pink face and a soft chin - "Hello, hello! I just finished checking the mess inside the body." "He was murdered, right?" Rowe asked eagerly.
[2205] "Yes."
[2206] "Yes, indeed. Of course, it's difficult to make a definite diagnosis based on the condition of the body, but I estimate that he died more than thirty-six hours ago, so he must have died around midnight on Sunday."
[2207] "Midnight on Sunday!" Percy glared at Roe, who glared back at her. Mr. Jury Ring shuddered.
[2208] "This is consistent with the time on the watch," the prosecutor concluded. "Twelve o'clock - twenty - six minutes. The watch must have stopped at the time of the murder. He was killed at zero point twenty-six on Monday."
[2209] The little bald man continued, "He was shot from the front, at close range. Three bullets." He dropped three deformed bullets on the table. "The slash on the case is strange. There is also a deep cut on the wrist. The beginning of the cut on the wrist is exactly where the slash on the case stops."
[2210] "In other words," Roe asked, "you think the same attack caused the cuts on both the wrist and the case?"
[2211] "That's the standard answer!"
